> 🚨 【JOE’S CRYPTO NEWS】
>
> 有「白毛股神」之稱的 Serenity 公開表示，其 AI 主題投資組合本月最大回撤達 49.4%。
>
> Serenity 指出，儘管短期市場大幅調整，但不會改變對 AI 基礎設施長期發展的看法。
>
> 其投資組合主要布局 AI 產業鏈的核心環節，包括：
>
> • 💾 Memory（存儲芯片）
> • 💡 Photonics（光子技術）
> • 🤖 Robotics（人形機器人）
> • 🖥️ 上游半導體產業鏈
>
> 他表示，這些高成長賽道在市場風險偏好下降時波動更劇烈，因此已主動降低槓桿，以控制投資組合風險。
>
> 市場持續關注 AI 產業鏈後續走勢，以及本輪調整是否將帶來新的布局機會。
>

### Photon Capital (@PhotonCap)
_Fri Jul 17 16:55:30 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 40 · ↻ 3 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/PhotonCap/status/2078161683923841073)

> Silicon cannot make light.
>
> You can build the modulators, waveguides, and detectors in silicon, but the light source still has to come from InP. So the more silicon photonics wins, the more InP sells. What looks like a materials war is a vertical division of labor.
>
> UMC and Tower both expanding 300mm on the same day just pulled that trade forward. The math is in the piece.
> $COHR $LITE $MTSI $AXTI

### Athu (@athuinvests)
_Fri Jul 17 19:16:58 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 81 · ↻ 4 · 💬 13 · [open on X](https://x.com/athuinvests/status/2078197286103113912)

> Portfolio up 45% YTD, down from the ATHs.
>
> The pullback has given me plenty of lessons that I’ll carry into the next leg up.
>
> A few I wanted to share:
>
> - Set a strict limit on % allocation to any single stock, even if conviction is 120%, mainly due to volatility and risks. Allocate more to less volatile or revenue-proven names. Big lesson on BALANCE.
>
> Example: $SIVE at 110 SEK felt fairly valued to me, and hitting my fair value range without trimming let it reach 40% of the portfolio. I’m still reflecting on that. As a 2027+ long, I stopped buying until 30 SEK recently. Would like a second opinion?
>
> - Know when to trim or add—not perfectly, since you can’t time the market—but having a process helps manage risk and allocate better (especially during bad sentiment periods like recently). Also keep more cash on hand. Big lesson on PATIENCE for me.
>
> Example: Could have added $AAOI lower than the $140–$150s. With $KXIAY, I could have added more slowly instead of all in during the dips (in terms of allocated capital). Lack of basic TA skills (which I’m building now) would have helped.
>
> That said, I remain heavily invested in the AI buildout and concentrated in a few sectors with stocks at 2x+ potential.
>
> That’s the risk I’m willing to take personally.
>
> Names:
> - Cloud: $NBIS, $BRUN
> - Compute/Packaging/Foundry: $INTC
> - Memory: $MU, $KXIAY, $MIRAE (Equipment/Test)
> - Photonics: $SIVE, $AAOI
>
> Decided that materials won’t be in my portfolio for now (no $AXTI, $SOI, etc.), unless I do swing trades. 👀 But still looking into an energy long. 😉
>
> In terms of diversification, I am opening up to another tech area like software/fintech or defense/space.
>
> Mag7? Not right now. Still young enough to take more risk.
>
> But again, tech or nothing! Mainly because I want to invest where I’m 120% convinced and understand the sector properly.

### Gaetano (@crux_capital_)
_Fri Jul 17 19:53:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 43 · ↻ 1 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/crux_capital_/status/2078206352414110036)

> Alright, let's start with $VIAV
>
> Market cap: ~$9.2B
> Next-quarter guide: ~$432M (+6.2% QoQ, +48.7% YoY)
> Next-12M revenue: $1.80-1.95B, 32-43% growth
> Exit margins: 63-64.5% gross, 24-26% operating
>
> VIAVI sits in the test layer for the optical buildout
>
> They touch many different stages of testing
>
> > During lab and product development
> > During manufacturing and production
> > During installation, operating, and field management
>
> They have very broad exposure in the data center:
>
> > Traditional pluggables
> > LPO, LRO, NPO, CPO, XPO 
> > AECs 
> > Retimers
> > PCIe 
> > CXL 
> > Hollow Core Fiber
>
> So they can test the silicon-photonics component, the optical engine, the packaged module, the Ethernet system, the physical fiber network, and the live AI fabric.
>
> One thing that I really like is that complexity increases test intensity. CPO, NPO, and advanced packaging create more testing insertions per system, so they can grow from both higher network volumes and more test content attached to each build.
>
> Also their Network and Service Enablement (NSE) segment has gross margins above 65%, with management estimating that roughly 40–45 cents of each incremental revenue dollar can reach operating profit.
>
> Some risks: Spirent integration, weak cash conversion/dilution, multiple compression, and delays in 1.6T/CPO customer ramps.
>
> *Reported growth includes the acquired Spirent product lines, which contributed $54.2 million last quarter, so don’t treat all of that growth as organic.
> *Margins / Rev are my projections 
>
> NFA

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Fri Jul 17 21:10:41 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 172 · ↻ 19 · 💬 13 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2078225902027108605)

> Morgan Stanley: Optical vs Copper
>
> How do you think about the optical scale up opportunity in 2027, 2028, 2029, etc, and how does that relates to the Nvidia ecosystem and roadmap?
>
> A: We believe a small scale out adoption next year, with small volumes accounting for 10-15% penetration with scale out. We do think there are some low adoption with CPO until Feynman in 2029. Small, single digit adoption of CPO in 2028 and really scaling in 2029.
>
> You took your TAM to $73B, 4x from a year ago, talk about the drivers of that and how that compares to consensus and buy side out there?
>
> A: Driven by CapEx data points being 2x we were expecting last year, that is one vector of growth. The other is the cluster sizes being discussed are the biggest rivers of scale up network . We have gone from 8 to 72, then from a couple 100s to 1000s in the next couple generations. This acts as a multiplier to scale up multiplier.
>
> Talk about the exposure among Lumentum, Coherent, and Corning. Are there nuances between who is more exposed, less exposed?
>
> A: For CPO within scale out, it is generally positive for Lumentum. Doesn't necessarily changed a whole lot for Corning. With Coherent, they have to balance it out with transceiver business they have. For Lumentum it is the most positive because of the one customer they have on the transceiver side being google and they are not going to be adopting CPO. For CPO within scale up, it is opportunity for all 3. This is where copper gets replaced with fiber and lit up by lasers and optical engines made by Coherent an Lumentum. In terms of overall exposure, Lumentum has a bigger catalyst because of larger AI/DC revenue. It would be incremental for both Coherent and lumentum. Lumentum #1, Coherent or Corning #2.
>
> Tell me about the Corning Glass Bridge announcement that got the stock excited?
>
> A: This is not a new announcement. It was a paper they released in 2025 and a presentation they did that refocused the market on this technology. It is already part of the $10B photonics target the company discussed couple of months ago.
>
> In terms of catalyst for optical space, OCP (Open Compute Project) coming in October has gone popular. What are you expecting to hear from this?
>
> A: We think this will be a catalyst because it provides more exposure into hyperscaler behavior. OCP will give us a chance to see hyperscalers roadmap, it will focus on CPO, NPO adoption and the vendors involved.
>
> Copper is still the story for 2026 and 2027. We have seen this continued enthusiasm for ASICs. How is copper well positioned for this dynamic? Who are the well positioned beneficiaries?
>
> A: Copper life can be extended with use of retimers and better SerDes. Copper has a lot of runway before switching to optics. We will likely see a hybrid environment before going to 100% optics. A large debate in scale up is what fabric and protocol will become dominant other than NVLINK as we get into new XPUs and alternatives to Nvidia GPUs ramping. A big debate here is between UALink and ethernet. Ethernet is dependent on Broadcom's new ASICs ramping in 2H2027 into 2028, we think Broadcom will have opportunity to bundle XPU solutions with networking portfolio and are very well positioned in ethernet. On UALink, this is high optionality for Marvell and Astera Labs. Astera has the scale up switch for Trainium 3, this is a PCIe based solution. We think customers will want to move to UA Link eventually.
>
> You consider Keysight as an agnostic winner in R&D, regardless of the copper vs optical timeline. Explain your thesis and why do you see it pulling ahead?
>
> A: Keysight really ways in multiple ways when it comes to AI. First, it benefits from different types of architectures being discussed which all need to be tested with their equipment in labs. Second, when you move to higher speeds (400g laser vs 200g), it requires more complicated testing. Third, when architectures change frequently, like every 2 years, that boosts their business. The variety of architectures being tested matters.
>
> $ALAB $NVDA $AVGO $MRVL $CRDO $SMTC $APH $KEYS $COHR $LITE $GLW $GOOGL

>
> Through fiber. 
>
> Through optical transceivers. 
>
> Through routers. 
>
> Through radio networks smart enough to handle loads that didn’t exist three years ago.
>
> That infrastructure doesn’t build itself.
>
> And the company quietly sitting at the center of all of it, making the optical transceivers, the IP routers, the radio access networks, and now an AI native 6G platform launched not to long ago,  is a Finnish company that most people dismissed a decade ago and haven’t looked at seriously since.
>

>
> Nokia booked €1 billion in AI and cloud orders in a single quarter. JPMorgan just raised their target from $14 to $21. Nvidia invested $1 billion at $6.01 a share, a price the stock has since blown past. AI and cloud revenue grew 49% year over year last quarter. Optical networks up 20%. Operating profit beat estimates by 12%. Guidance raised. Network Infrastructure growth forecast doubled.
>
> Two days ago Nokia launched its AI RAN platform, a radio access network built natively for artificial intelligence that thinks and adapts in real time. Their CEO called it one of the most significant advancements in radio technology in decades.
>
> And Nokia makes their own indium phosphide lasers in house. In Pennsylvania. In a facility just expanded 10x. Every competitor buys their lasers. Nokia makes theirs. That distinction matters more every quarter as supply chain sovereignty becomes a national priority.
>
> Q2 earnings are July 23rd. Six days away. First report where the Nvidia partnership shows up in order books. First report where the Allentown photonics expansion starts contributing. First look at whether the €1 billion in Q1 optical orders is the floor or the ceiling.
>
> The data has to move somewhere.
>
> I believe $NOK Nokia is where it moves.

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Fri Jul 17 22:17:49 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 135 · ↻ 25 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2078242798571049071)

> Goldman Sachs: Innolight & Optical Modules
>
> Market Trends and Technology Migration
>
> > Speed Evolution: The industry is aggressively migrating toward higher-speed optical modules. 1.6T modules are moving toward volume production as the next mainstream standard, while 3.2T optical modules are expected to begin volume ramp-up in 2027.
>
> > Silicon Photonics (SiPh) Dominance: Silicon photonics is increasingly displacing traditional EML-based solutions due to lower power consumption, superior performance, and simplified packaging.
>
> > Penetration Rates: By 2026, SiPh penetration is projected to reach 60% for 800G, 80% for 1.6T, and 100% for 3.2T products.
>
> > Revenue Share: Silicon photonics' share of total optical module revenue is expected to surge from 28% in 2025 to 62% by 2028.
>
> Innolight Shipment and Market Share Highlights
>
> > Leadership: Innolight is the leading supplier of 1.6T pluggable modules. It is projected to hold a 50–60% market share of 1.6T modules in 2026. Other industry reports indicate Innolight's market share for 1.6T modules may reach as high as 50–70%.
>
> 1.6T and 3.2T Outlook:
>
> > 1.6T: Expected to become the "absolute mainstream" by 2027, with 45.72 million units projected to be shipped that year.
>
> > 3.2T: Following the ramp-up of 1.6T, 3.2T shipments are expected to double in 2028 compared to their initial volume ramp year in 2027.
>
> > Manufacturing & Capacity: To support this demand, Innolight planned a 155% year-on-year increase in capital expenditure for 2026 to expand production capacity.
>
> Market Dynamics: Volume, Revenue, and ASP
>
> > Speed Migration (Volume Mix): The market is shifting rapidly from legacy "Below 400G" speeds toward high-speed AI-focused modules. 
>
> While "Below 400G" accounted for 89% of shipment volume in 2025, that share is projected to decline to 77% by 2028E. 
>
> Conversely, high-speed modules are capturing significant volume: 1.6T modules are projected to grow from 1% of volume in 2025 to 10% by 2028E, and 3.2T modules are expected to reach 5% of total shipment volume by 2028E.
>
> > Average Selling Price (ASP) Trends: The report explicitly notes an assumed year-over-year (YoY) ASP decline for "like-for-like" products. 
>
> For example, the ASP for 1.6T modules is expected to drop from $840 in 2025 to $435 by 2028E. 
>
> The 3.2T module, which enters the market in 2027, has a high starting ASP of $1,023 in 2027E, which is then projected to decline to $768 by 2028E.
>
> Technological Shift: SiPh vs. EML
>
> > Silicon Photonics (SiPh) Adoption: The market is undergoing a significant transition from traditional EML-based materials to Silicon Photonics.
>
> SiPh revenue penetration is expected to increase from 28% in 2025 to 62% by 2028E.
>
> Correspondingly, the SiPh penetration rate (by volume) is projected to climb from 6% in 2025 to 18% by 2028E.
>
> Market Opportunity (TAM)
>
> > Total Addressable Market (TAM): The global optical module TAM is expected to grow from $34.2 billion in 2025 to a peak of $72.6 billion in 2027E, before moderating slightly to $69.1 billion in 2028E.
>
> > High-Speed Revenue Growth: The 1.6T and 3.2T segments represent the primary growth engines, with combined revenue for these categories projected to grow from $3.9 billion in 2025 to $44.9 billion in 2028E.

### mark (@cherryPayment)
_Fri Jul 17 22:38:17 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 9 · ↻ 0 · 💬 6 · [open on X](https://x.com/cherryPayment/status/2078247946894622934)

> 我认为是很合理的分析
>
> 首先我们需要知道底层逻辑为什么英飞拓可以作为行业晴雨表？
>
> 我们要知道英飞拓是全球最大光模块厂商之一，它的ASP走势和出货量确实能反映整个产业链的景气度。高盛这样的机构是不会无缘无故上调108%/119%的盈利预测，那么其背后一定有channel check支撑。
>
> 所以基于此我是倾向于把英飞拓理解为光子行业的”台积电”。
>
> 而这个逻辑是台积电的资本开支指引和产能扩张节奏，是整个半导体行业景气度的先行指标；同理，英飞拓的订单结构、ASP走势和产能规划，是光子产业链景气度的先行指标。当英飞拓的盈利预测被机构上修超过100%，这不仅仅是一家公司的好消息——这是整个生态的信号弹。
>
> 800G超预期这个信号很关键。800G目前仍是主力交付速率，超预期意味着数据中心扩建节奏比市场预期快，这对LITE这类以800G为主的厂商是直接利好。
>
> 1.6T/3.2T拉高ASP的逻辑也成立，更高速率产品单价更高，即使出货量不变，收入和毛利都会改善。
>
> 高盛预期英飞拓在硅光（Silicon Photonics）模块的出货量将显著超出此前预期。这背后是三个维度的需求同步爆发：
>
> •Scale Out（横向扩展）：更多GPU集群节点互联，需要更多光模块
>
> •Scale Up（纵向扩展）：单节点算力密度提升，对高速互联带宽需求更高
>
> •Scale Across（跨域扩展）：数据中心之间、城域网之间的互联需求增加
> 这三个维度的同步扩张，意味着光模块不再只是某一个场景的刚需，而是AI算力基础设施全面扩张的基础组件。
>
> 2. 1.6T/3.2T产品拉高ASP和利润率
> 光模块产品的迭代路径是：400G → 800G → 1.6T → 3.2T。更高速率的产品，单价更高，毛利率通常也更好。
> 1.6T和3.2T产品的加速渗透，意味着即使英飞拓的出货量增速放缓，其收入和毛利仍会因为产品结构升级而显著改善。这是一个量价齐升的逻辑——在AI Capex持续扩张的背景下，这个趋势有望延续至2028年。
>
> 3. AI Capex的持续扩张
>
> 微软、Google、Meta、亚马逊等全球四大超大规模云厂商的2025年资本开支指引，无一例外都在大幅提升。这些资金最终会流向哪里？算力芯片、服务器、网络互联设备——以及连接这一切的光模块。
>
> 英飞拓作为这条链条中最关键的环节之一，是AI Capex最直接的受益者之一。
>
> 所以我认为在方向正确 + 间接收益方面 ：我是倾向于 $soi 和 $sive的

### Investor Denis (@InvestorDenis)
_Fri Jul 17 23:05:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 23 · ↻ 6 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/InvestorDenis/status/2078254671198638361)

> Just found new evidence the US government is dead serious about developing quantum technologies.
>
> US research is funded partly through the National Science Foundation (NSF). If your grant application is approved, you receive money.
>
> The NSF launched an initiative called NSF X-Labs two months ago. The goal of the initiative is to fund teams of researchers, engineers, and entrepreneurs to solve specific scientific challenges.
>
> The funding available is $1,5 billion over the next decade.
>
> The first round of X-Labs couldn’t have been more explicit. It invited proposals on two topics:
>
> 1/ Scientific instrumentation for sensing and imaging (deadline for grant applications: July 13)
>
> 2/ Quantum systems: Interconnects and integrated photonics (deadline July 20)
>
> The initiative resonates with
>
> 1/ the $2 billion direct equity investment into nine quantum companies in May
>
> 2/ the Executive Orders on quantum in June that look to find companies capable of providing these technologies, e.g. $INFQ and $IONQ.
>
> It’s hard not to be bullish on a technology pushed by the US government.

### นักลงพุง (@naklongpoong)
_Fri Jul 17 23:32:05 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/naklongpoong/status/2078261485424304227)

> ตลาด Optical Module กำลังเข้าสู่ยุค 1.6T และ 3.2T พร้อมแรงหนุนจาก Silicon Photonics
>
> Goldman Sachs ระบุว่า อุตสาหกรรม Optical Module กำลังเร่งเปลี่ยนผ่านไปสู่โมดูลความเร็วสูงเพื่อรองรับการเติบโตของ AI Data Center โดย 1.6T กำลังก้าวขึ้นเป็นมาตรฐานหลักของตลาด ขณะที่ 3.2T จะเริ่มเข้าสู่การผลิตจำนวนมากในปี 2027
>
> การเปลี่ยนผ่านสู่ Optical Module ความเร็วสูง
>
> อุตสาหกรรมกำลังเร่งเปลี่ยนจากโมดูลรุ่นเดิมไปสู่ความเร็วที่สูงขึ้น
>
> 1.6T กำลังเข้าสู่การผลิตจำนวนมาก และจะกลายเป็นมาตรฐานหลักของตลาด
> 3.2T คาดว่าจะเริ่มผลิตในระดับ Mass Production ตั้งแต่ปี 2027
> Silicon Photonics กำลังแทนที่ EML
>
> Goldman Sachs มองว่า Silicon Photonics (SiPh) จะเข้ามาแทนเทคโนโลยี EML (Electro-Absorption Modulated Laser) อย่างต่อเนื่อง เนื่องจากมีข้อได้เปรียบหลายด้าน ได้แก่
>
> ใช้พลังงานต่ำกว่า
> ประสิทธิภาพสูงกว่า
> กระบวนการประกอบแพ็กเกจง่ายกว่า
>
> อัตราการใช้งาน SiPh ที่คาดการณ์
> 800G: 60% ภายในปี 2026
> 1.6T: 80%
> 3.2T: 100%
>
> ขณะที่สัดส่วนรายได้ของ Silicon Photonics จะเพิ่มจาก 28% ในปี 2025 เป็น 62% ภายในปี 2028
>
> Innolight ครองตลาด 1.6T
>
> Goldman Sachs ระบุว่า Innolight เป็นผู้นำตลาด Optical Module แบบ 1.6T Pluggable
>
> คาดว่าจะมีส่วนแบ่งตลาด 50–60% ในปี 2026
>
> ขณะที่รายงานจากแหล่งอื่นประเมินว่าส่วนแบ่งตลาดอาจสูงถึง 50–70%
>
> แนวโน้ม 1.6T และ 3.2T
>
> 1.6T
> คาดว่าจะกลายเป็นมาตรฐานหลักของอุตสาหกรรมภายในปี 2027
> ยอดจัดส่งปี 2027 คาดอยู่ที่ 45.72 ล้านโมดูล
>
> 3.2T
> หลังจาก 1.6T เริ่มแพร่หลายแล้ว
> ยอดจัดส่ง 3.2T ในปี 2028 คาดว่าจะเพิ่มขึ้นเป็น 2 เท่า ของปีแรกที่เริ่มผลิตในปี 2027
>
> เพื่อรองรับความต้องการดังกล่าว Innolight วางแผนเพิ่ม CapEx ปี 2026 ถึง 155% YoY เพื่อขยายกำลังการผลิต
>
> การเปลี่ยนแปลงของตลาดและ ASP
>
> ตลาดกำลังเปลี่ยนจาก Optical Module ความเร็วต่ำ ไปสู่ผลิตภัณฑ์สำหรับ AI อย่างรวดเร็ว
>
> สัดส่วนยอดจัดส่ง
> โมดูลต่ำกว่า 400G จะลดจาก 89% ในปี 2025 เหลือ 77% ในปี 2028
> 1.6T จะเพิ่มจาก 1% เป็น 10%
> 3.2T จะเพิ่มเป็น 5% ของยอดจัดส่งทั้งหมดภายในปี 2028
>
> ด้านราคาขายเฉลี่ย (ASP)
> Goldman Sachs คาดว่าราคาจะปรับลดลงตามการผลิตจำนวนมาก
>
> 1.6Tปี 2025: 840 ดอลลาร์
> ปี 2028: 435 ดอลลาร์
>
> 3.2Tปี 2027: 1,023 ดอลลาร์
> ปี 2028: 768 ดอลลาร์
>
> การเปลี่ยนผ่านจาก EML ไปสู่ SiPh
> ตลาดกำลังเปลี่ยนผ่านจาก EML ไปสู่ Silicon Photonics อย่างชัดเจน
> สัดส่วนรายได้ของ SiPh จะเพิ่มจาก 28% ในปี 2025 เป็น 62% ในปี 2028
> ส่วนแบ่งการใช้งานตามปริมาณ (Volume Penetration) จะเพิ่มจาก 6% เป็น 18% ในช่วงเวลาเดียวกัน
>
> โอกาสของตลาด (TAM)
>
> Goldman Sachs คาดว่ามูลค่าตลาด Optical Module ทั่วโลกจะเติบโตอย่างแข็งแกร่ง
> 2025: 34.2 พันล้านดอลลาร์
> 2027: 72.6 พันล้านดอลลาร์ (จุดสูงสุด)
> 2028: 69.1 พันล้านดอลลาร์
>
> ขณะที่รายได้จากกลุ่ม 1.6T และ 3.2T ซึ่งเป็นแรงขับเคลื่อนหลักของอุตสาหกรรม จะเพิ่มจาก
> 3.9 พันล้านดอลลาร์ในปี 2025
> เป็น 44.9 พันล้านดอลลาร์ในปี 2028

### Lon Forehand (@LonForehan)
_Mon Jul 20 16:16:16 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/LonForehan/status/2079238972274868686)

> A lab at Sandia National Laboratories just found a new strategy for controlling light. No human designed the experiment that found it.
>
> If you run any kind of research or technology organization, that sentence should be sitting uncomfortably in the back of your planning assumptions right now.
>
> Sandia scientists built what the field calls a self-driving lab — a closed-loop system where AI designs experiments, robotics runs them, and AI reads the results and designs the next one. The system isn't executing a pre-written protocol. It's building the protocol as it goes. And in the domain of optics and photonics, it returned with a novel light-control strategy the human researchers hadn't specified in advance.
>
> Here's the part that matters for anyone with a five-year research roadmap: the self-driving lab doesn't just run known experiments faster. It explores the space between the experiments a human team would have prioritized. It goes places humans don't have bandwidth to go. That's a different category of capability than "AI-assisted workflow."
>
> Photonics isn't niche — it's the foundation of fiber communications, lidar for autonomous vehicles, medical imaging, and solar energy systems. A new light-control strategy found autonomously has downstream implications across a dozen industries that are still treating AI adoption as a measured, multi-year transition.
>
> The full piece on Substack is written directly to R&D directors, lab chiefs, and technology organization leaders — as a letter, not a lecture. It asks one genuinely hard question about your planning horizon and works through what the honest answer requires. Including the strongest case for why autonomous labs are still limited, and why that case actually sharpens the urgency rather than softening it.
>
> After the article, Claude reviewed it independently and added its own labeled response. "The harder and more interesting question is whether the self-driving lab architecture can be extended to messy domains — not whether it can be deployed to easy ones."
>
> Read my full argument on Substack below and Claude's response. https://t.co/dzAtCM1DX7

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNrwc3TXoAAqVYF.jpg

### The Alpha Centauri (@theACentauri)
_Mon Jul 20 16:20:09 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 66 · ↻ 2 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/theACentauri/status/2079239951191826461)

> Побачити планету біля чужої зорі — задача на межі неможливого. Якщо планета в зоні придатності, вона тулиться близько до світила, а те світить приблизно в 10 мільярдів разів яскравіше. Стівен Айкенберрі, професор і керівник проєкту в оптичному коледжі Університету Центральної Флориди (CREOL), описує це так: спробуйте розгледіти крихітний блимаючий вогник, коли вам в обличчя б'є прожектор.
>
> Астрономи вже гасять це сяйво коронографом — приладом, що перекриває диск зорі й пропускає до детектора слабкий сигнал планети. Та мікроскопічні дефекти оптики пропускають частину зоряного світла крізь усю систему. "Скажете — це ж одна мільйонна частка", — каже Айкенберрі. "І що? Зоря все одно в 10 тисяч разів яскравіша за вашу екзопланету. Вам кінець."
>
> Проєкт PEEPSS (Photonics-Enabled Exoplanet Spectroscopic System) ловить ці спотворення там, де їх раніше не міряли — у фокальній площині, тій самій точці, де формується наукове зображення. Більшість систем стежить за хвильовим фронтом раніше в оптичному тракті й не бачить помилок, що виникають уже після коронографа. Їх називають аберраціями неспільного шляху: світло проходить ділянку, яку не контролює жоден датчик.
>
> Серце проєкту — фотонний ліхтар. Пристрій розкладає вхідне світло на окремі оптичні канали й відновлює не лише яскравість, а й фазову інформацію хвиль — дані, які звичайні детектори просто стирають. Завдяки цьому відкривається "квантово-натхненне зображення", де поведінка світла підвищує роздільність і відфільтровує рештки зоряного сяйва. Передову роботу над такими ліхтарями у світі ведуть лише два центри — UCF та Університет Сіднея.
>
> Підтверджених екзопланет уже понад 6 000, та пряме зображення досі бере хіба що газові гіганти розміром з Юпітер на далеких орбітах — землеподібні світи надто тьмяні. Технологію готують для майбутньої обсерваторії HWO (Habitable Worlds Observatory), флагманського телескопа NASA з дзеркалом 6–8 метрів для пошуку двійників Землі. Трирічний проєкт будує й тестує прототипи, а деякі версії вже випробували на телескопах на Гаваях. Айкенберрі формулює ставку прямо: "Ми за одну місію від відповіді. Підведемо очі — і знатимемо."
>
> https://t.co/x9A1YQAkpL

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNrxtv2XkAAjJPR.jpg

### mark (@cherryPayment)
_Mon Jul 20 16:45:45 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 105 · ↻ 15 · 💬 8 · [open on X](https://x.com/cherryPayment/status/2079246395517833360)

> 其实我们去看 $LITE 的市值变化会发现很有趣的事情：二十五年前它在泡沫里亏掉560亿，在25年初市值仅60亿美金，今天它却值六七百亿，而去研究他的发家史，我会不自觉的套用到 $sive身上。
>
> 2001年，一家叫JDS Uniphase的光通信巨头，一年亏了大约560亿美金。真金白银的年度亏损，上一轮互联网泡沫最大的墓碑之一。
>
> 今天我聊它是想去看懂这一轮AI里最容易被忽略的那条暗线；二是说句实话，我在拿它当一面镜子，去对照我最喜欢的一家公司 $SIVE。
>
> 这条暗线是：所有人都在抢光模块，可那颗藏在光模块里、最难造、连英伟达都得排队抢的激光芯片，是它供的。做光模块的公司被当"卖铲人"炒。可光模块拆开，里面那颗叫EML的铟磷激光心脏，五到六成出自Lumentum。它是卖铲人的卖铲人，那么硬到什么程度？2026年3月，英伟达直接掏20亿美金入股它、外加一份数十亿的采购大单，就为把它的激光产能提前锁死。全世界最懂算力供需的那家，用钱投了一票"这颗芯片会长期缺"。
>
> 但我更想让你注意的是它年轻时候的样子，因为它不是暴发户，是熬了几十年的老鬼。
>
> 1979年就有的血统，1999年合并成JDSU是那轮光纤狂欢里最亮的星，然后泡沫破了，亏掉560亿。2015年，它被当成一块"不性感的器件厂"分拆出来单过——给电信商供激光器、给苹果供Face ID的激光点阵，收入不小，故事平平，没人给估值。
>
> 接下来那十年才是关键。它趴在冷板凳上，靠一串"补器官"式的收购一块一块把造高端激光器需要的硬骨头焊进自己家：2018年吞Oclaro拿下相干光、2022年买NeoPhotonics拿下超窄线宽激光、2023年收Cloud Light一脚踏进数据中心光模块。到2023年底，家底攒齐了，可市值还只有35亿美金，没几个人拿正眼看它。
>
> 然后2025年2月，一个在光通信圈摸爬滚打小半辈子的老兵接过方向盘。几个月后，AI这阵风吹来了。结果就是那根鞭子：从2023年底约35亿，到2026年中六七百亿，不到三年，翻了18到20倍。
>
> 那就很好奇了它凭什么能被一把抡起来？
>
> 它是少数几个"手里真有货"的人。这十年的攒货，我在文里从头捋到尾。
>
> 现在说第二件也是我今天想聊的。
>
> Lumentum年轻时候那个样子，和我买入的 $SIVE 现在像得让我后背发凉。
>
> 它俩做的是同一层的活：光互联最上游那颗铟磷激光光源。摩根士丹利那份"激光供应"名单本来就把SIVE和 $lite、 $COHR 归在一起。区别只在于时间——Lumentum是"跑通之后"的样子，SIVE是它十年前那个"手里正在攒货"的样子。
> 而且别以为SIVE是个刚冒头的初创。它真正对标Lumentum的那条激光光源命脉——Sivers Photonics，前身叫CST Global——是2001年从苏格兰格拉斯哥大学分拆出来的，做铟磷/DFB激光已经二十五年了，2016年就能月产上百万颗DFB激光器。Sivers这家公司2018年上了纳斯达克北欧的First North、2021年登上斯德哥尔摩主板。
>
> 不知道你看出来了吗：Lumentum是四十年的老手，SIVE的激光那条线也是二十五年的老手。 两个都不是暴发户，都是在这颗又脆又难的铟磷激光上磨了大半辈子的匠人：一个已经等到了风，一个还在等。这才是我把它俩摆在一起的真正原因。
>
> 你把两条路叠一起看，相似的地方太多了：
>
> 一样是那颗最难的InP激光光源、一样是几十年的老手；一样是小市值、没人看好、故事还没被主流讲透；一样在闷头攒家底——Lumentum当年靠收购，SIVE现在靠融资扩产能、靠一个个设计导入把自己焊进下一代CPO；也一样，都在等那个能把它一把抡起来的临界点。
>
> Lumentum的临界点是英伟达那20亿 + AI那阵风。而SIVE 还在等它自己的那阵风，而目前我认为风来了（那一笔融资）
>
> 所以Lumentum这条18倍的路对我判断SIVE有两层意义：它先替我证实了这条赛道到底值不值钱（值），又告诉我SIVE想复制它，还差哪几步。我把SIVE现在走到了哪一格、还欠着哪几张"兑现凭证"，画成了一张LITE照SIVE的对照图——具体哪几步，我留在文里，这里先不摊。
>
> 我前几天算SIVE从10亿到100亿是10倍。听着激进？可Lumentum刚刚当着所有人的面，走完了18到20倍。有些倍数，不是幻想，是已经发生过的先例。
>

> 完整的来时路、它到底跟谁在合作、以及那张LITE照SIVE的对照图，都在这一篇里。

> $LPTH Continues to Gain Wall Street Support as Demand for Advanced Optics Accelerates
>
> As AI infrastructure expands beyond chips and data centers, another segment of the supply chain is attracting growing attention: precision optics and photonics.
>
> That’s one reason Craig-Hallum has reiterated its Buy rating on $LPTH, while Wall Street’s consensus price target stands at $16.17, implying meaningful upside from the stock’s recent close of $10.53.
>
> AI Hardware Requires More Than Just GPUs
>
> Building AI infrastructure isn’t only about faster processors.
>
> Modern AI systems also depend on advanced optical technologies used in:
>
> High-speed data communications
> Infrared imaging
> Autonomous systems
> Aerospace and defense
> Industrial sensing
> Semiconductor manufacturing
>
> As computing power increases, demand for precision optical components continues to grow across multiple industries.
>
> This creates a favorable backdrop for companies like Lightpath Technologies.
>
> Revenue Is Growing Rapidly
>
> Lightpath’s latest quarterly results showed significant top-line momentum.
>
> Compared with the same quarter last year:
>
> Revenue increased from $9.17 million to $19.15 million, more than doubling year over year.
> However, the company still reported a GAAP net loss of $4.11 million, compared with a $3.58 million loss a year earlier.
>
> The results suggest that while demand is improving, the business is still investing heavily to support future growth.
>
> Profitability Remains the Next Milestone
>
> Like many smaller technology companies, Lightpath is still in an investment phase.
>
> Revenue growth is encouraging, but investors will ultimately want to see:
>
> Improving gross margins
> Better operating leverage
> Reduced cash burn
> A clearer path toward consistent profitability
>
> Strong revenue alone is unlikely to sustain a higher valuation if losses continue to widen.
>
> Insider Selling Deserves Context
>
> One factor investors may notice is recent insider activity.
>
> A director-affiliated investment fund recently sold approximately 3.57 million shares, worth about $50 million.
>
> Large insider sales often attract attention, but they don’t necessarily indicate deteriorating business fundamentals.
>
> Institutional funds may sell for reasons unrelated to the company’s outlook, including portfolio rebalancing, fund liquidity, or investment lifecycle considerations.
>
> Investors should watch whether management’s operational execution continues to improve rather than relying solely on insider transactions.
>
> My View
>
> Lightpath sits in an interesting niche of the AI ecosystem.
>
> While companies like $NVDA and $AMD provide the computing power, optical technologies are becoming increasingly important for moving data efficiently, supporting advanced sensors, and enabling next-generation AI hardware.
>
> The company’s strong revenue growth suggests demand is improving, but the next stage of the investment story will depend on translating that growth into sustainable profits.
>
> If management can continue expanding sales while improving margins, $LPTH could become one of the lesser-known beneficiaries of the broader AI infrastructure buildout.
>
> $LPTH $NVDA $AMD $LITE $COHR $GLW $AVGO

### GUL (@gulVasikova)

> $LWLG Strengthens Leadership With Veteran CFO as It Prepares for the Next Phase of Growth
>
> $LWLG announced the appointment of Fred Graffam as its new Chief Financial Officer, bringing more than 20 years of financial leadership and extensive public company CFO experience to the photonics company.
>
> While a CFO appointment doesn’t change the company’s technology overnight, it often signals that management is preparing for the next stage of corporate growth, partnerships, and investor engagement.
>
> Graffam has led finance organizations at several public companies, including Fidium (formerly Consolidated Communications), Ascent Capital Group, Brinks Home Security, and DigitalGlobe, where he helped oversee strategic transactions and corporate sales. His background also includes leadership roles at Level 3 Communications, Comcast, and Deloitte.
>
> CEO Yves LeMaitre said Graffam’s experience in financial operations, capital allocation, and communicating with Wall Street will help support the company’s long-term strategy and create shareholder value.
>
> Graffam also expressed confidence in Lightwave Logic’s future, describing the company as being at a “significant inflection point.” He believes its proprietary electro-optic (EO) polymer technology could play an important role in next-generation optical networking as AI drives demand for faster, lower-power data transmission.
>
> Why It Matters
>
> As AI models become larger and data centers continue to scale, moving information efficiently is becoming just as important as increasing computing power.
>
> Lightwave Logic is developing electro-optic polymers that convert electrical signals into optical signals with higher speed and lower power consumption than conventional technologies. If successfully commercialized, the technology could improve optical interconnects used in AI servers, networking equipment, and telecommunications infrastructure.
>
> However, investors should remember that $LWLG remains an early-stage technology company. The long-term opportunity depends on converting years of research into commercial products, customer agreements, and sustainable revenue.
>
> My View
>
> A new CFO doesn’t immediately change the investment thesis, but hiring an executive with significant public company and M&A experience is generally a positive step. It suggests management is strengthening its leadership team as the company moves closer to potential commercialization and deeper engagement with customers and investors.
>
> Ultimately, the biggest catalysts for $LWLG will still be commercial partnerships, customer adoption, licensing agreements, and revenue growth. If the company can successfully translate its photonics technology into real-world deployments, it could become a niche beneficiary of the expanding AI networking and optical communications market.
>
> $LWLG $POET $LITE $COHR $NVDA $AVGO $AMD

### GUL (@gulVasikova)
_Mon Jul 20 18:15:20 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/gulVasikova/status/2079268939071373344)

> Optical Networking Stocks Rally as AI Demand Remains Strong Despite Recent Pullback
>
> AI optical networking stocks moved higher on Monday after Barclays said the recent sector correction presents a potential buying opportunity rather than a deterioration in fundamentals. The firm believes demand for AI networking infrastructure remains robust as hyperscalers continue expanding next-generation AI data centers.
>
> Leading the rally were $LITE (+8%), $COHR (+5.7%), $MRVL (+3%), $AAOI (+2%), and $GLW (+1%). According to Barclays, the long-term growth drivers for optical components—including optical transceivers, lasers, photonics, and high-speed networking equipment—remain firmly intact as AI clusters become larger and require significantly greater bandwidth between GPUs.
>
> The investment thesis is straightforward: AI models are becoming larger, requiring tens of thousands of GPUs to communicate with one another. As compute capacity scales, networking becomes just as important as the chips themselves. Every new AI data center requires enormous amounts of optical connectivity, benefiting companies that supply the critical infrastructure linking GPUs together.
>
> Within this ecosystem, Lumentum and Coherent supply advanced optical components and lasers, Marvell provides AI networking silicon and custom connectivity chips, Applied Optoelectronics manufactures high-speed optical transceivers, while Corning supplies the fiber-optic infrastructure supporting AI networks. Together, these companies represent key beneficiaries of the global AI infrastructure buildout.
>
> Meanwhile, $NOK also attracted investor attention after SEB Equities upgraded the stock to Buy ahead of earnings on July 23. Options activity turned moderately bullish, with call volume significantly exceeding puts, although elevated implied volatility suggests traders expect a sizable post-earnings move. Options markets are pricing roughly a 12.5% move in either direction, reflecting uncertainty around the upcoming results.
>
> For Nokia, the long-term opportunity extends beyond traditional telecom equipment. The company has been expanding its portfolio in 5G, fiber broadband, cloud networking, private wireless networks, and AI-driven network infrastructure. As AI data centers and cloud providers require faster, lower-latency connectivity, Nokia’s networking technologies could become increasingly relevant alongside traditional telecommunications spending.
>
> The broader long-term thesis for the optical networking sector remains compelling. AI infrastructure investment is no longer focused solely on GPUs; networking, fiber, switching, and optical interconnects are becoming essential bottlenecks as hyperscalers build increasingly larger AI clusters. If AI capital expenditure remains elevated over the next several years, companies supplying these networking technologies could benefit from a sustained multi-year upgrade cycle.
>
> The primary risks include slower AI infrastructure spending, customer concentration among hyperscalers, pricing pressure, and the cyclical nature of semiconductor and networking equipment demand. However, as AI workloads continue growing, optical networking remains one of the most important enabling technologies supporting the next generation of AI infrastructure.
>
> $LITE $COHR $MRVL $AAOI $GLW $NOK $NVDA

### ImNotHarsh | 📈💸 (@imnotharsh)
_Mon Jul 20 18:22:26 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 27 · ↻ 3 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/imnotharsh/status/2079270725232349468)

> $INTC Intel were the first to mass produce integrated photonics modules for data centers. 
>
> Intel continues to develop advancements in integrating lasers and optics into silicon using standard chip manufacturing.
>
> Intel Labs pioneered silicon photonics to meet the growing demand for more efficient and resourceful network infrastructure for ever-increasing amounts of data. Commercialization of prototypes has transferred to Intel’s data center business, and with more than six million Intel 100G transceivers and integrated lasers in use, Intel is paving the way for next-generation deployments and future innovations.
>
> Photonics offers superior reach, bandwidth density, power consumption, and latency in high-speed networks and provides rack-to-rack connectivity for data center applications, including optical communications and telecommunications. Integrated photonics brings together the advantages of silicon photonics and CMOS circuits. By integrating the power of optical directly with compute, memory, and peripheral technologies, high bandwidth data can be moved throughout the entire network with significantly less power.
>
> Integrated photonics research at Intel Labs is focused on reducing costs, size, and operating power, and extending optical performance to enable more scalable, disaggregated architectures at the highest level of the network. Core technology building blocks under development include light generation, amplification, detection, modulation, CMOS interface circuits, and package integration technology.

### GUL (@gulVasikova)
_Mon Jul 20 18:35:51 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/gulVasikova/status/2079274102167376329)

> $LASR Sets August 6 Earnings Date as Investors Watch Defense Laser and Directed Energy Momentum
>
> $LASR announced it will report second-quarter 2026 financial results after the market closes on August 6, followed by a conference call with management to discuss the company’s performance and outlook.
>
> While the announcement itself is routine, the upcoming earnings report comes at an important time as investors increasingly focus on companies supplying technologies for directed energy weapons, optical sensing, and advanced defense systems.
>
> Why Investors Are Watching
>
> nLIGHT is one of the few publicly traded companies specializing in high-power semiconductor and fiber laser technologies used across defense, industrial manufacturing, aerospace, and sensing applications.
>
> Its vertically integrated platform allows the company to manufacture critical laser components—from semiconductor chips to complete laser systems—giving it greater control over performance, cost, and product development.
>
> The company’s defense business has become an increasingly important growth driver, particularly as governments accelerate investment in laser-based air defense, counter-drone systems, missile defense, and next-generation military technologies.
>
> Long-Term Investment Thesis
>
> The global defense industry is undergoing a major shift toward directed energy weapons, with lasers expected to play an increasingly important role in protecting military bases, naval vessels, armored vehicles, and critical infrastructure from drones, rockets, and missiles.
>
> Unlike traditional kinetic interceptors, laser weapons offer several advantages:
>
> Extremely low cost per shot.
> Near-instant engagement speed.
> Deep ammunition capacity limited primarily by available electrical power.
> Reduced logistics requirements compared with conventional missile systems.
>
> As these systems move from testing into broader deployment, demand for high-performance laser technology could increase substantially.
>
> Beyond defense, nLIGHT also serves industrial markets including precision manufacturing, semiconductor production, additive manufacturing, and advanced sensing, providing additional sources of long-term growth.
>
> What to Watch on August 6
>
> Investors will focus on:
>
> Defense revenue growth and contract pipeline.
> Updates on directed energy programs.
> Gross margin improvement.
> Orders and backlog trends.
> Commercial laser demand.
> Management’s full-year outlook.
> Progress on new product development.
>
> Any commentary regarding defense spending, AI-enabled battlefield technologies, or partnerships with major defense contractors could be closely watched.
>
> Risks
>
> Like many specialized photonics companies, nLIGHT faces risks including customer concentration, government procurement timing, project delays, competitive pricing, and the cyclical nature of industrial capital spending.
>
> Defense programs also often have long procurement cycles, meaning revenue growth can be uneven from quarter to quarter.
>
> Bottom Line
>
> The August 6 earnings report will provide investors with an updated view of demand across both the defense and industrial markets. As governments continue investing in directed energy weapons, counter-drone technologies, and next-generation military systems, nLIGHT remains well positioned as a supplier of the high-power laser technologies that underpin these emerging platforms.
>
> If management delivers improving margins, growing defense orders, and a strong outlook, it could reinforce the long-term thesis that directed energy is becoming a major pillar of future defense modernization.
>
> $LASR $LMT $RTX $NOC $LHX $AVAV $KTOS

>

>
> 8. 📉 Trump ponownie zapowiedział możliwość zaostrzenia polityki handlowej wobec partnerów USA, co zwiększa niepewność wokół światowego handlu i łańcuchów dostaw.
>
> 9. 🏭 Europejskie giełdy rozpoczęły tydzień spokojnymi wzrostami, a inwestorzy oczekują serii wyników finansowych największych spółek oraz kolejnych danych makroekonomicznych.
>
> 10. ⚡ Nastroje na rynku pozostają ostrożnie optymistyczne, jednak inwestorzy uważnie śledzą rozwój sytuacji geopolitycznej oraz możliwe zmiany w polityce handlowej USA.

### SoFire (@Sofigoodboy)
_Mon Jul 20 22:53:42 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Sofigoodboy/status/2079338992072523995)

> 1. No Signal Issue: The arriving 2 mW easily exceeds the receiver sensitivity requirement (0.2 dBm), ensuring flawless data transmission.
>
> 2. Standard Physics: A ~21.6 dB optical loss is standard across Silicon Photonics (SiPh) architectures, including legacy pluggable transceivers.
>
> 3. Net Energy Winner: The small power increase for a stronger laser is far outweighed by eliminating power-hungry DSPs, driving down overall system power.
>
> 4. Improving Losses: Next-gen innovations like edge couplers and TFLN modulators are continuously pushing these link loss numbers even lower.

### The Lucky Lighthouse (@Lkylighthouse)
_Mon Jul 20 23:11:02 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 7 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Lkylighthouse/status/2079343352655536550)

> AXTI / Tongmei: The Thesis Is Stronger but More Specific
>
> AXTI / Tongmei should be underwritten as an upstream InP capacity-conversion investment.
>
> Demand has been materially validated.
>
> The unresolved question is whether Tongmei can convert that demand into permitted, qualified, margin-positive shipments before competing capacity expands and scarcity economics normalize.
>
> That is a stronger thesis than “AI demand is growing.”
>
> It is also a more demanding one.
>
> What matters next
>
> The next decisive datapoints are:
>
> * export-permit cadence,
> * confirmation of prepayment receipts,
> * 6-inch qualification progress,
> * InP revenue mix,
> * inventory and contract-liability treatment,
> * gross-margin durability, and
> * the handling of Tongmei’s listing and redemption obligations.
>
> Bottom line: the thesis remains intact and is commercially stronger. The risk has shifted from proving demand to proving execution.

### Wind Info (@WindInfoUS)
_Mon Jul 20 23:36:17 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/WindInfoUS/status/2079349708070543786)

> Wind Financial Morning Post: July 21, 2026
>
> Market Brief
>
> Concerning the expansion and quality improvement of the service sector and the planning and construction of the "Six Networks," the State Council Executive Meeting has issued its latest directives.
>
> The National Development and Reform Commission held a private enterprise symposium, revealing key macroeconomic policy priorities for the second half of the year.
>
> The State Council Information Office held a press conference to introduce the development of industry and information technology in the first half of the year.
>
> The China Securities Regulatory Commission held an investor symposium to hear opinions and suggestions.
>
> LPR remained unchanged for the 14th consecutive month; monetary policy may be strengthened in the second half of the year.
>
> U.S. forces launched a new strike against Iran; mediators proposed a 10-day ceasefire between the U.S. and Iran.
> The United States announced additional 50% tariffs on certain Canadian products.
>
> Britain's new Prime Minister Burnham's debut: to launch the largest reform in 40 years and reshape the economic model.
>
> Top Stories
>
> On the morning of July 20, Wu Qing, Chairman of the China Securities Regulatory Commission, conducted a field visit to a securities branch in Beijing and chaired an investor symposium, engaging in face-to-face exchanges with eight representatives including large, medium, small, and retail investors to solicit opinions and suggestions on promoting the stable and healthy development of the capital market. Wu Qing stated that investors are the foundation of the market and the most important participants in the capital market. The CSRC will adhere to an integrated approach to prevent risks, strengthen regulation, and promote high-quality development of the capital market, fully safeguarding market stability, enhancing the transparency and authenticity of listed companies, delivering better returns to investors, urging industry institutions to operate in compliance and improve investor services, continuously improving long-term investor protection mechanisms, and resolutely maintaining an open, fair, and just market order to enable investors to better share the fruits of high-quality economic and capital market development.
>
> The State Council Information Office held a press conference to introduce the development of industry and information technology in the first half of the year. The Ministry of Industry and Information Technology stated that it will issue and implement industry-specific and thematic 15th Five-Year Plan guidelines for the industrial and information technology sector; continue implementing new rounds of growth-stabilization action plans for industries such as machinery and automobiles to comprehensively expand high-quality supply and effective demand; will issue guidelines for the construction of computing power standard systems and promote the establishment of standards for market-based computing power pricing; accelerate the cultivation of emerging growth points such as photonics and spatiotemporal information and speed up the implementation of integrated computing-power layouts; will expedite the issuance of the "AI + Software" action plan.
>
> U.S. forces launched a new strike against Iran. President Trump posted on social media, suggesting that U.S. forces would launch a strong retaliatory action against Iran following recent casualties. The Iranian Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps stated that it struck U.S. military targets in Bahrain and Kuwait in three phases. A senior Iranian official said mediators have proposed a 10-day ceasefire to discuss reviving the temporary agreement between Iran and the United States. Iranian Foreign Ministry Spokesperson Baghaei confirmed receipt of the mediator's proposal, stating that negotiations with the United States depend on whether they align with Iran's national interests.
>
> Britain has seen its seventh prime minister in ten years. Andy Burnham, newly elected leader of the ruling Labour Party, was appointed by the British monarch as the new prime minister and authorized to form a new cabinet. 
>
> Andy Burnham delivered a speech pledging to end a decade of political turmoil in Britain, implement the "largest reform in 40 years," and reshape the country with a new economic model, with a ten-year economic recovery plan to be released before the end of this year.
>
> China Macro & Policy
>
> Premier Li Qiang presided over a State Council Executive Meeting, hearing reports on inspections of the expansion and quality improvement of the service sector and the planning and construction of the "Six Networks"—water networks, new power grids, computing power networks, next-generation communication networks, urban underground utility networks, and logistics networks. The meeting approved the "15th Five-Year Plan for Intellectual Property Protection and Utilization," studied relevant work on optimizing the social security system, and heard recommendations on rectifying issues identified in the 2025 audit of central budget execution and other fiscal revenues and expenditures. The meeting emphasized the need to systematically advance the planning and construction of the "Six Networks," accelerate implementation according to local conditions and industry needs, strengthen financial and elemental support, and ensure the effective construction of major infrastructure networks.
>
> Zheng Shanjie, Chairman of the National Development and Reform Commission, presided over a private enterprise symposium to solicit opinions and suggestions on the economic situation in the first half of the year and economic work for the second half. Zheng stated that the NDRC will leverage the combined effect of existing and new policies, accelerate the cultivation of new consumption growth points, continuously promote the implementation of major projects outlined in the 15th Five-Year Plan outline, facilitate smooth transitions between old and new growth drivers, accelerate the development and opening of application scenarios, further build a high-quality data supply system, and deepen the construction of a unified national market.
>
> Lin Jian, spokesperson for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, presided over a regular press briefing. Lin stated that summit diplomacy plays an irreplaceable strategic guiding role in China-U.S. relations, and both sides have maintained communication regarding summit interactions this year.
>
> A symposium for leading officials of industrial and information technology authorities across the country was held in Beijing. The meeting emphasized strengthening legislative research and reserves in emerging fields such as digital economy, artificial intelligence, and low-altitude economy, intensifying efforts to rectify "cutthroat" competition, and continuously fostering a first-class business environment characterized by marketization, rule of law, and internationalization.
>
> The Ministry of Commerce convened a national video conference to advance mid-year work on the policy for replacing old consumer goods with new ones. The meeting stressed the need to implement the policy meticulously, further intensify efforts to expand its coverage, optimize the subsidy review and disbursement process, facilitate public participation and benefit, and enhance public satisfaction.
>
> The State Administration for Market Regulation issued the "Action Plan for Promoting Platform Enterprises to Empower Individual Businesses," proposing that by the end of 2027, a series of "five batches" of achievements will be continuously formed to explore long-term practical pathways for platform enterprises to empower individual businesses. The Action Plan deploys five special actions: startup support, key cultivation, capability enhancement, digital empowerment, and innovation demonstration.
>
> The PBOC announced the July LPR rates: 3% for the one-year term and 3.5% for terms longer than five years, unchanged from June, in line with market expectations. Since the 10-basis-point cut in May 2025, the LPR has remained unchanged for 14 consecutive months. Although the July LPR held steady, the PBOC has repeatedly emphasized the implementation of a moderately loose policy. Industry experts generally anticipate a possible 5- to 10-basis-point reduction in the second half of the year, primarily based on room left by the PBOC's moderately loose policy, potential declines in banks' liability costs, and possible underperformance of economic data or the real estate market.
>
> Data released by the National Bureau of Statistics showed that in June, the unemployment rate for urban non-student labor aged 16–24 was 14.9%, down 0.7 percentage points from the previous month; the unemployment rate for urban non-student labor aged 25–29 was 7.1%, down 0.1 percentage point; the unemployment rate for urban non-student labor aged 30–59 was 4.0%, down 0.1 percentage point. Unemployment rates for all three age groups have declined for three consecutive months.
>
> China Equities Markets
>
> On Monday, China's three major stock indices opened higher and fluctuated, briefly turned negative in the afternoon, then slightly recovered by the close. The SSE Index rose 0.85% to 3,796.28 points, the Shenzhen Component Index fell 0.71%, the ChiNext Index rose 0.42%, and the Wind All China Index fell 0.69%. Oil and gas, power, and coal stocks strengthened; liquor stocks were active; large financial stocks rose collectively; the computing power hardware industrial chain continued to adjust. Total market turnover reached 2.72 trillion yuan, compared with 2.67 trillion yuan the previous day.
>
> The Hang Seng Index closed up 2.36% at 25,143.05 points, the Hang Seng Tech Index rose 2.79%, and the Hang Seng China Enterprises Index rose 3.01%. Tech stocks broadly advanced; energy and innovative pharmaceutical concepts performed strongly; AI large model leaders declined, with Zhipu falling over 19% and MiniMax falling over 10%. Total market turnover was HK$306.4 billion, with Southbound funds net selling HK$5.962 billion.
>
> The Hong Kong Stock Exchange responded to market rumors about considering extending stock trading hours and eliminating the lunch break, stating that it is currently studying multiple measures to enhance market convenience, including extending trading hours, but its primary focus is currently on studying proposals to extend derivatives market trading hours, not stock trading hours.
>
> Citigroup revised its emerging markets asset allocation recommendation, upgrading China's equity market rating to "overweight." Citigroup strategists set a target price of $92 for the MSCI China Index by the end of 2026, implying a potential upside of 31%.
>
> China Industry News
>
> The Ministry of Commerce and eight other departments issued the "Several Policy Measures to Promote the High-Quality Development of the Domestic Care Services Industry," increasing support for domestic care enterprises, guiding them to participate in the construction of long-term care service systems, and supporting qualified domestic care providers to offer home-based long-term care insurance services. The policy encourages domestic care platform enterprises to support flexible employment care workers in joining employee pension and medical insurance schemes through methods such as "individual voluntariness + platform subsidies."
>
> The State Administration for Market Regulation and three other departments issued the "Guiding Opinions on Comprehensive Governance and Regularized Supervision and Enforcement of Fuel Pump Fraud," requiring accelerated implementation of smart metering supervision for fuel pumps, encouraging local governments to explore new models of smart metering supervision, promoting local governments to issue policy documents to advance smart metering supervision, strengthening the construction of digital and intelligent supervision platforms for refined oil circulation, and promoting "transaction and invoicing simultaneously" at all retail fuel stations.
>
> The National Energy Administration issued a document requiring the construction of a number of village and town micro-energy network pilot projects nationwide by the end of 2028; by the end of 2030, successful experiences and mature models from pilot projects should be effectively implemented in rural areas.
>
> Boeing forecasts that global airlines will require nearly 44,000 new aircraft over the next 20 years, with China, the Middle East, Latin America, South Asia and Southeast Asia, and Africa accounting for approximately 55% of new aircraft deliveries; aviation freight volume is expected to grow at an annual rate of about 3.7% through 2045, outpacing trade growth.
>
> Fintech
>
> The People's Bank of China Beijing Branch announced its disapproval of Beijing KUBao Payment Technology Co., Ltd.'s application to change its registered capital. This is the first case this year in which a payment institution's capital increase was rejected by regulators. KUBao Payment currently has a registered capital of 100 million yuan and faces a capital shortfall of 115 million yuan; its license expires on December 21, 2026. Failure to successfully increase capital before then may affect license renewal.
>
> Corporate News & Updates
>
> Alibaba Cloud launched a lightweight application server instance dedicated to AI agents, bundling vCPUs, memory, cloud disks, 200 Mbps peak bandwidth (with zero traffic fees), and AI model tokens (ranging from 100 million to 3.2 billion) into prepaid packages to provide users with an integrated AI agent operating environment. The service is currently available in 12 regions including Beijing, Shanghai, and Guangzhou, with plans to expand to more domestic and overseas regions. Meanwhile, Alibaba Cloud adjusted its sales strategy for intelligent outbound call agents: starting July 30, 2026, the minimum specification for new purchases and renewals of intelligent outbound call agents will be uniformly set at 100,000 minutes.
>
> https://t.co/zDq3KwGBbd officially implemented three core upgrades for its cross-border tax refund services—fully paperless processing, payment via overseas bank cards, and "buy now, refund immediately." JD Pay's "link overseas card to domestic account" became a key component of this upgrade, further streamlining the entire process for overseas travelers from payment to tax refund completion, enabling full transaction and refund processing with a single overseas card.
>
> Hon Hai Precision Industry received its first artificial intelligence server assembly order from SpaceX, with the transaction value potentially reaching as much as $52 billion. SpaceX plans to order approximately 13,000 NVIDIA GB300 server racks from Hon Hai, with each rack estimated to cost $4 million. Hon Hai expects to begin shipments in the fourth quarter of this year and continue through the first quarter of next year.
>
> Amazon Global Selling launched the "Flagship New Seller Incubation Program," with its first goal of helping 2,000 new Chinese brands listed on Amazon achieve individual brand sales exceeding 100 million yuan over three years by 2029. The program provides customized overseas expansion solutions for manufacturers, brand owners, and emerging brands targeting markets in North America, Europe, Japan, and beyond.
>
> Novo Nordisk announced that the European Commission has granted marketing authorization for Wegovy® tablets (semaglutide tablets). With this approval, Wegovy® tablets become the first tablet-form GLP-1 receptor agonist approved for weight management in all EU member states and the fifth global market to grant registration approval, following the United States, the United Kingdom, the United Arab Emirates, and Bahrain.
>
> Global Macro & Policy
>
> The White House stated that President Trump signed a proclamation authorizing the Secretary of Commerce to establish an incentive program to support enterprises investing in aluminum smelters. The incentive program requires companies to submit "industrial repatriation plans." Approved companies may import primary aluminum at corresponding quotas and benefit from reduced tariff rates equivalent to half the rate under Section 232.
>
> The United States will impose an additional 50% ad valorem tariff on certain Canadian products to address "discriminatory measures by Canada on U.S. automotive and automotive parts trade." The new tariffs will take effect at 00:01 Eastern Daylight Time on August 19 and will be levied in addition to existing tariffs, duties, and other charges.
>
> The U.S. Bureau of Economic Analysis plans to revise its statistical methods for investment management services, computer software, and legal services. The updated methods will be introduced alongside the August inflation data on September 30 and will be applied retroactively to the past five years. This may make inflation figures later this year appear slightly lower.
>
> The Houthi movement in Yemen announced a maritime navigation ban against Saudi Arabia in response to Saudi Arabia's "unjust and brutal blockade and aggression."
>
> Benefiting from semiconductor seasonal demand boosting exports, South Korea's per capita GDP is expected to reach $39,164 this year, an increase of $2,750 year-over-year, or 7.6%, the highest since 2021. If the average annual exchange rate of the Korean won against the U.S. dollar remains below 1,456.1 won, South Korea's per capita GDP is expected to enter the "$40,000 era."
>
> Global Equity Markets
>
> The three major U.S. indices closed slightly lower. The Dow Jones Industrial Average fell 0.59% to 51,839.26 points, the S&P 500 fell 0.19% to 7,443.28 points, and the Nasdaq Composite fell 0.05% to 25,508.07 points. The Wind US Magnificent Seven Index rose 0.09%; Microsoft rose over 2%, and Google rose over 1%. SpaceX fell over 3%. The Nasdaq Golden Dragon China Index rose 0.9%; Kingsoft Cloud rose over 5%, and Alibaba rose over 4%. Optics communication and storage sectors mostly rose; SanDisk and Western Digital rose over 2%.
>
> The three major European indices closed mixed. Germany's DAX rose 0.06% to 24,846.69 points, France's CAC 40 rose 0.02% to 8,340.11 points, and the UK's FTSE 100 fell 0.71% to 10,524.76 points. Escalating Middle East tensions pushed oil prices higher, reviving inflation concerns; market sentiment remained cautious ahead of the European Central Bank's key meeting.
>
> The KOSPI closed down 4.46% at 6,516.27 points; SK Hynix and Samsung Electronics both fell over 4%. Citigroup downgraded its Korea market rating from "overweight" to "tactical neutral," citing market volatility and KOSPI implied volatility far exceeding global peers. Morgan Stanley also lowered its bear-case target for the KOSPI index from 6,500 to 6,000 points. Japanese markets were closed for Ocean Day. India's SENSEX 30 fell 0.57% to 77,708.52 points.
>
> The Thailand Securities and Exchange Commission stated that Thailand plans to launch a new individual tax-exempt savings account this year to encourage long-term investment in stocks, bonds, and mutual funds and to bolster personal retirement reserves. The account will be modeled after Japan's NISA: individuals investing at least 600,000 Thai baht (approximately $17,822) annually will qualify for tax benefits, guiding residents to convert more savings into long-term financial assets.
>
> Samsung Biologics announced it has launched a full-cash tender offer to acquire the Swiss PolyPeptide Group, with a transaction value of 1.46 billion Swiss francs (equivalent to $1.8 billion). The transaction is expected to close by the end of this year. Samsung Biologics stated that this acquisition will become the largest biopharmaceutical merger and acquisition in Korean history.
>
> Bonds
>
> China's interbank bond market fluctuated and adjusted; yields on major government bonds mostly rose slightly, with longer-term maturities (five years and above) showing weakness. Government bond futures declined collectively; the 30-year main contract fell 0.16%. The PBOC conducted 398.5 billion yuan in reverse repurchase operations, net injecting 174.5 billion yuan, but liquidity in the interbank market remained tight, with the DR001 weighted average rate rising 1 basis point to above 1.41%, while DR007 edged lower and hovered around 1.43%.
>
> Panda bond issuance exceeded 160 billion yuan in the first half of the year, up nearly 70% year-over-year; as of the end of June, cumulative issuance surpassed 1.3 trillion yuan, with over 110 issuers from 24 countries and regions across five continents.
>
> TSMC plans to issue its third unsecured ordinary corporate bond of the year, with a total issuance amount of 18.5 billion New Taiwan dollars, expected to be completed in July. According to the prospectus, the bond is divided into two tenors: a 5-year bond with an issuance amount of 14 billion New Taiwan dollars and a coupon rate of 2.03%; a 10-year bond with an issuance amount of 4.5 billion New Taiwan dollars and a coupon rate of 2.10%.
>
> U.S. Treasury yields rose across the board: the 2-year yield rose 2.96 basis points to 4.204%, the 3-year yield rose 3.67 basis points to 4.249%, the 5-year yield rose 4.09 basis points to 4.319%, the 10-year yield rose 4.22 basis points to 4.592%, and the 30-year yield rose 4.45 basis points to 5.112%.
>
> Commodities
>
> International precious metals futures closed mixed: COMEX gold futures fell 0.17% to $4,011.80 per ounce, while COMEX silver futures rose 0.60% to $56.66 per ounce. Escalating U.S.-Iran conflict boosted risk aversion, but uncertainty around Federal Reserve policy reforms remains, and elevated U.S. Treasury yields have yet to ease, resulting in divergent market movements amid bullish and bearish pressures.
>
> U.S. crude oil futures rose 0.78% to $82.42 per barrel; Brent crude futures rose 0.81% to $88.81 per barrel. Escalating tensions in the Middle East and U.S.-Iran conflict, with the United States stating Iran will pay a price for U.S. military deaths, and Houthi forces backed by Iran announcing a maritime navigation ban against Saudi Arabia threatening Red Sea crude export routes, combined with U.S. strategic petroleum reserves reaching their lowest level since 1983, have narrowed global crude supply buffers, supporting oil prices.
>
> Most London base metals closed lower: LME copper rose 0.88% to $13,644.50 per ton, LME tin rose 0.11% to $53,290.00 per ton, LME zinc fell 0.30% to $3,515.00 per ton, LME nickel fell 0.30% to $16,910.00 per ton, LME lead fell 0.32% to $1,877.00 per ton, and LME aluminum fell 0.46% to $3,136.00 per ton.
>
> Indonesia's B50 palm oil-based biodiesel policy has succeeded; the country will completely halt diesel imports starting July 2026. Halting diesel imports will bring substantial economic benefits to the population, and the government plans to redirect fiscal funds previously used for overseas fuel purchases directly into the domestic agricultural industry.
>
> Goldman Sachs believes that if Middle East conflicts further escalate and intensify inflation and rate hike concerns, copper prices may face downside risks in the short term. Goldman Sachs expects copper markets outside the United States to remain tight in the near term.
>
> FX & Currency Markets
>
> On Monday, the onshore yuan closed at 6.7670 per U.S. dollar at 16:30, up 103 basis points from the previous trading day; the night session closed at 6.7690. The PBOC's central parity rate was set at 6.7948, down 14 basis points from the previous day.
>
> At the close of New York trading, the U.S. dollar index rose 0.20% to 100.97; most non-U.S. currencies rose: the euro fell 0.20% to 1.1414 against the dollar, the pound fell 0.16% to 1.3431, the Australian dollar rose 0.24% to 0.6999, the dollar rose 0.06% to 162.5020 against the yen, the dollar rose 0.33% to 1.4067 against the Canadian dollar, the dollar rose 0.36% to 0.8103 against the Swiss franc, and the offshore yuan rose 90 basis points to 6.7692 against the dollar.

### Nirmātṛ (@En_formare)
_Mon Jul 20 23:50:21 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/En_formare/status/2079353247597523395)

> Silicon photonics just scored the ultimate material remix – micro-transfer printing (MTP) is the nanoscale stamp wizard letting engineers graft InP lasers, GaAs mode-lockers, and lithium niobate modulators onto silicon nitride platforms like precision stickers, finally busting CMOS out of its group-IV straitjacket for the AI data deluge.
>
> Instead of forcing silicon to do everything alone (and failing at efficient light generation or high-speed electro-optics), engineers pre-fabricate “coupons” on source wafers with sacrificial layers, suspend them on tethers, then use a PDMS elastomeric stamp to peel and print them onto target wafers at room temperature with ≤0.5 µm 3σ alignment accuracy.
>
> High-tech Lego for photons; offering high material efficiency, known-good-die selection, zero solder parasitics, and far-back-end compatibility that keeps the CMOS kitchen cool while the fancy guests bring the performance. MTP delivers wafer-scale heterogeneous integration that beats flip-chip (too parasitic), die-to-wafer bonding (lower throughput), and epitaxial growth (lattice mismatch and high-temperature incompatibility).
>
> Recent demos include InP tunable lasers on SiN with 25 kHz linewidth, 54 nm C+L band tuning, and 6.3 mW output; GaAs continuous-wave and mode-locked lasers pumping >4 mW at 3.2 GHz repetition; thin-film LiNbO₃ push-pull Mach-Zehnder modulators hitting 70 GHz bandwidth and 3.2 V·cm Vπ; and the first LiTaO₃ modulators on silicon photonics via the same stamp process. 
>
> Throughput already reaches 45-second cycles and scales with parallel reticle-level printing toward thousands of devices per hour on 200 mm wafers, record territory for hybrid photonic engines.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNtYwVYawAE-8PY.jpg

Foundries worldwide stand to gain as photonic chiplets become the new normal for AI infrastructure. The stamps are ready.

### Arvind Srinivas (@glocalinvestor)
_Sun Jul 19 13:04:27 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 5 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/glocalinvestor/status/2078828314584568029)

> I have no disagreements here with @michaelsikand 
>
> One additional very important Caveat I would like to add is, multi decade AI buildout doesn’t mean winners are obvious today. 
>
> Heck for all we know the real winners aren’t even visible yet. Thematic success and a company success are two very different things. 
>
> $SIVE or $AAOI or $CRDO or $COHR might be the poster child for photonics today but for all we know right now, they might not be there to see photonics win. Execution is of paramount importance and surprisingly few are actually good at it. 
>
> All I can tell is keep watching the moves, follow the earnings, keep questioning the thesis and never borrow conviction. 
>

That's a classic sign of multiple compression rather than a broken investment thesis.
>
> This is also not happening in isolation. Momentum funds are unwinding crowded AI positions, ETFs have been rebalancing following Russell reconstitution, macro investors are rotating around Fed expectations and geopolitical risks, while short sellers have become increasingly vocal after one of the strongest AI rallies in history. $SPY $QQQ $VIXY $SOXX 
>
> these flows can overwhelm fundamentals for weeks..
>
> Meanwhile, the data that actually matters continues pointing in the opposite direction. Hyperscalers are expected to spend more than $700 billion on AI infrastructure this year, $TSM still says AI demand exceeds supply, $NVDA continues expanding networking capacity and optical content per AI cluster keeps increasing as GPU deployments scale toward hundreds of thousands of accelerators.
>
> I think the market is once again pricing the next headline instead of the next earnings report. I've seen this movie before with DeepSeek, valuation scares, recession fears etc..
>
> Different narrative, same outcome. Until AI capex, customer orders and earnings start rolling over, I see this as another healthy reset inside a secular AI infrastructure supercycle, not the end of it.

### LearnInvest (@LearnInvest2026)
_Sun Jul 19 13:20:52 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/LearnInvest2026/status/2078832445688889555)

> AI's next optical bottleneck may be the laser
>
> Citi estimates that data-center demand for continuous-wave laser chips will reach about 223 million units in 2026 against supply of roughly 198 million. By 2028, demand approaches 990 million while supply reaches about 638 million. Under that model, demand would exceed supply by 55%.
>
> ■ Bandwidth upgrades move the bottleneck into light sources
>
> As AI clusters shift from 800G to 1.6T links, switches and GPUs require more high-speed optical connectivity. Silicon photonics can integrate modulation and transmission, but it still needs reliable indium-phosphide lasers as the light source. Wider adoption of co-packaged and near-packaged optics increases the number of sources required across the system.
>
> Supply is expanding. Coherent has moved a six-inch indium-phosphide platform into volume production, allowing more chips per wafer, while other vendors are adding capacity. Yield, packaging, and customer qualification can still limit the ramp even after factory space is added.
>
> This is a demand scenario, not a shortage already guaranteed to happen. Shipments of 800G and 1.6T equipment, six-inch wafer yields, laser pricing, and lead times will test the forecast. A slower demand ramp or faster yield improvement would rewrite the 55% gap.
>
> Source: Citi Research and Coherent OFC 2026 Investor Event (Image: @pequityresearch)

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNl_F__WUAAH7-J.jpg

> 最近のアナリストによる325ドルから350ドルへの引き上げは、株価30%の調整にもかかわらず、Credoがより広範なAI接続プラットフォームへと移行していることを裏付けています。
>
> より遅いコパッケージ光学機器の採用はAECの滑走路を延ばし、CPOは2026年に浸透率が0.5%にとどまると予測されています。
>
> 光ネットワーク市場は2031年までに230億ドルから1120億ドルへと拡大し、複数の成長サイクルを支える見込みです。
>
> コンセンサスでは、2031会計年度までに収益が24.5億ドルから67.8億ドルに増加すると予想されており、現在のプレミアム評価はますます妥当に見えるように見えます。
> ------------------------------------------------------------
> 1. 株価30%下落でも事業の強さはむしろ確認された
> 6月高値から30%以上下落したが、事業悪化の兆候はなし。
>
> 下落要因は「マクロ環境・利益確定」であり、ファンダメンタルはむしろ強化。
>
> 2. アナリスト評価が一斉に上方修正
> Evercore：$325
>
> Stifel：$350
>
> Bank of America：$340   → いずれも現在のコンセンサスを大きく上回る。 → 理由は「Credo が AEC企業ではなく AI接続プラットフォームへ進化している」点。
> 3. CPO（コパッケージ光学）の普及遅れはむしろ追い風
> 2026年のCPO浸透率は 0.5% に留まる見通し。
>
> Copper（AEC）需要が長期化し、Credoの既存製品の収益機会が拡大。
> Jensen Huang も「次世代AIシステムは copper と optics の両方が必要」と明言。
>
> 4. 光ネットワーク市場は 2031年までに 23B → 112B へ拡大
>
> CAGR 30% の巨大成長市場。
>
> 800G / 1.6T、シリコンフォトニクス、CPOなど複数の成長サイクルが連続する。
> 5. 同業他社も高成長 → 構造的なインフラ投資サイクル
>
> Astera Labs：+93%
>
> Lumentum：+90%   → 単なる在庫積み上げではなく、本物のAIインフラ投資サイクル。
> 6. 高いバリュエーションは「割高ではなく妥当」
>
> EV/Sales：15.2x
> P/E：33.9x
>
> EV/EBITDA：28.7x → 一見高いが、
> 売上は FY2027：2.45B → FY2031：6.78B（+177%）
> PEG：0.75x（Broadcomと同水準）
> Astera Labsよりはむしろ割安 → 複数の成長サイクルを持つ企業として妥当。
> 7. 強気シナリオの鍵は「プラットフォーム化」
>
> Copper / Optics / Silicon Photonics / Software / Memory Connectivity → これらを単一製品ではなくスタックとして採用できるかが重要。

> 顧客集中（Hyperscaler依存）
> 光学製品の立ち上がり遅延
> 高バリュエーションゆえの実行リスク
> 8. 結論
>
> Credoは「光学企業」ではなく、 AIインフラ全体を貫く接続プラットフォーム企業へ進化中。 この構造的な変化は市場にまだ十分織り込まれておらず、 長期的なアップサイド余地は大きいという評価。

### Pep Invest (@PepInvestStocks)
_Sun Jul 19 15:32:12 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 79 · ↻ 10 · 💬 6 · [open on X](https://x.com/PepInvestStocks/status/2078865496242586009)

> $GFS long-term relationship with $SIVE did not begin with the recent AI photonics announcements, it started years earlier with an investment that, in hindsight, illustrates how deep-tech ecosystems are built.
>
> Long before $SIVE acquired MixComm in 2022 for approximately $135 million, $GFS recognized the startup’s potential in millimeter-wave RFIC technology.
>
> Rather than limiting the relationship to that of a manufacturing partner, $GFS took an early minority equity stake in MixComm while closely aligning the company’s designs with its proprietary RF-SOI (Silicon-on-Insulator) process technology.
>
> The move reflected a broader strategy: combining capital investment with manufacturing expertise to help accelerate technologies that could create long-term demand for $GFS specialized semiconductor platforms.
>
> The 2022 acquisition of MixComm by $SIVE marked an important turning point.
>
> Instead of exiting its investment entirely, $GFS chose to convert its ownership in MixComm into publicly traded shares of $SIVE.
>
> That decision distinguished $GFS from purely financial investors.
>
> By maintaining an equity position beyond the transaction and after the lock-up period, the company signaled confidence not only in $SIVE immediate 5G opportunities but also in the broader technology roadmap the combined business could pursue.
>
> Looking back from 2026, that strategy appears increasingly significant.
>
> Technologies originally developed to address high-frequency wireless communications are now finding applications well beyond the 5G market.
>
> As artificial intelligence drives unprecedented demand for faster and more energy-efficient data center infrastructure, photonic interconnects have emerged as one of the industry's most important growth areas.
>
> Against this backdrop, the AI photonics collaboration announced by $GFS and $SIVE in June 2026 represents more than a new commercial partnership.
>
> It reflects years of strategic alignment built through technology development, manufacturing collaboration, and equity ownership.
>
> By combining $SIVE advanced laser technology with $GFS high-volume silicon photonics manufacturing platform, the companies are targeting one of the key challenges facing next-generation AI data centers: enabling scalable, high-bandwidth optical connectivity while improving power efficiency.
>
> In an industry where partnerships often evolve as quickly as technology itself, sustained equity ownership can provide valuable insight into long-term strategic priorities.
>
> $GFS continued position as a shareholder suggests that its original investment in MixComm was never solely about participating in the 5G cycle.
>
> Instead, it formed part of a broader vision, one that has evolved from millimeter-wave communications to the rapidly expanding AI photonics ecosystem now shaping the future of hyperscale computing.
